Irwin's new 
art at UCSD 
continued from paCle 1 

During this time he 
participated in sensory 
deprivation experiments. In 
these experiments, you learn 
that if you momentarily cancel 
your focus on your self you will 
become more sensitive to the 
surrounding environment. This 
caused a shift in Irwin's art from 
looking at art as an object in a 
gallery to using art as a method 
of affecting our perception of 
the gallery itself, The gallery 

that light. but you 're already on 
your way back into the world. So 
you swing harder and you get a 
little higher and you see a little 
more, but back into the world 
you go, To recognize something 
and then live there takes a 
tremendou conversion of your 
being. You don 't just swing up 
there and ay 'Oh, that's nice; 
and stay there, hanging in mid 
air. Nanging in mid air can bt. 
nice, but the world always draws 
you back. 

The ordinary, could we but 
see it. is just as extraordinary as 
the highest consciousness 
available." 

One can phy ically exit 

Irwin's installation, but what w 
learn about our perceptions, 
and the heightening of the 
perceptions will never exit from 
our being. Hi installation of 
stainless steel and cyclone 
fencing into the forest is a 
metaphor for the expanded 
framework he has installed into 
our minds, 

Irwin 's scu lpture also draws 
our attention to the need and 
value of public art. Within our 
mass-market sl ick -packaged 
cloned society, we have lost the 
"art" in our culture. Before 
World War II , people 
experienced art in every aspect 
of th ir live. From the bas-

. 

relief culptures carved into 
architecture to the embroidery 
on a shirt or dress, from the 
paintings in a church to the 
handmade craftsmanship in 
household furnishings, people 
lVere aware that a quality 
existed in things, 

The name of this quality was 
Art. The war de troyed our belief 
that things could endure from 
generation to generation 
because of its quality, So we 
stopped crea ting objects of 
quality and started mas -
producing flashy throwaway . 
Art was cloistered away to the 
white-wall galleries of New York 
for some future renaissance . 

A renaissance is a rebirth. 
Here at UCSD the " Museum 
Without Walls " will be a rebirth 
of Art into our liv s, We won 't 
need to travel to some East 
Coast gallery to experience art; 
it will be available on the 
pathway of our daily journ y , 
The Art may first seem like a 

tranger, whom we may like or 
dislike. But as we become more 
familiar with Art w will start 
allowing Art to come into our 
lives as a quality friend. With 
time, friends start to ab orb 
each other's qualities and 
characterist ics, With time, we 
too will be able to accentuate 
our life with art.

centering around the struggle for power. In it. a

bringing back traditional values. Written in 
1965, Tango is as relevant today as it was in the

Vis. Arts students will 
be featured this week 

The works of new graduate 
students in the Department of 
Vi ual Arts at UCSD ar featured 
In an exhibit ion entitled " 18 
Arti ts Come to San Diego." in 
the Mandeville Ann x Gallery. 

" 18 Artists Come to San 
Diego" i curated by the 
sludents themselves. The work 
in this show renects widely 
divergent approaches lo su~ect 
matter and media, due in part to 
the artistic concerns that each 

'artist has brought from different 
parts of the country. Visitors to 
the exhibition will find work 
from several regional traditions. 
Students have come to UCSD 
from Chicago, New York, San 
f'rancisco, Sacramento , 
Montreal. Minnesota and 

Mississippi. One student is from 
Sweden. 

The media in which these 
tudcnts work range from 

'iCulpture to painting to film, 
video and photography. Most of 
the work is a co mbination of 
these genres. 

The arti!>ls represented in this 
exhibit ion are MilT lene Al t

Selling your photos is the 
topic of extension class 

Nationally-known freelance 
photographer Rohn Engh will be 
here this weekend to present a 
speC Ial UCSD Extension 
program titled "How to Sell 
Your Photographs." 

Scheduled for 7-10 p.m. 
Friday, and from 9 a.m.-4:30 
p.m. Saturday and Sunday, in 
UH 104, the program costs $85. 

Engh studied at the Maryland 
Institute of Design in Baltimore 
and as a freelance photographer 
has sold his work to such 
publications as Ifarper 's, 
Woman ' Day, and Reader's 
Digest 

He is the publisher of The 
Photofetter. a newsletter for 
freelance photographers. and 

, , 

the author of the book 110w to 
Self and Resell Your Photos. 

In his UC D Extension 
program, Engh will cover the 
difference between "good" 
photographs and marketable 
ones, formulas for producing 
marketable pictures every time, 
service photography versus 
photo illustration, finding your 
corner of the market. dealing 
with editors, pricing pictures. 
packaging, selling yourself: 
assignments, stock photo and 
advertising agencies, photo-
decor, copyrights, tax shelters, 
and the portfolio. 

For information on 
enrollment. call UCSD Extension 
at 452-3400.

C}tl[ presents. acoustic duo Sat. 

The. James fmery / Robert Dick Duo will perform at UCSD Saturday. 

Weekend offers two 
concerts of interest 

The La Jolla Civic / University 
orchestra and chorus will 
perform their second concert of 
the season Saturday and 
Sunday. The concert is devoted 
to music based on Jewish 
tradition. 

Music Director Thomas Nee 
will conduct Ernst Bloch 's 
Concerto gross for strings. and 
Bloch 's " Shelomo. " Hebrew 
Rhapsody for cello and 
orchestra . featuring Milton 
Saier as soloist. Choral 
conductor David Chase will 
present Leonard Bernstein 's 
"Chichester Psalms" for chorus 
and orchestra. besides two 
songs for a-capella choir: A 
traditional Sabbath tlymn 
arranged by Dudley Cohen and a 
Renaissance Motet with Hebrew 
text by Salomone Rossi. 

Saturday's performance will 
be at 8 p.m. in Mandeville. 
Sunday's concert begins at 3 
p.m. at the Congregational 
&th-EI on Gilman Drive. For 
more information ca ll 452-
1734. 

---

The " End of Quarter " 
concerts at the UCSD Music 
Department end with a Chamber 
Ensembles program. friday. at 8 
p.m .. in Mandeville Auditorium. 

A recently formed Chamber 
Orchestra of 16 instruments -
mainly strings - dedicated to 
classical music. will play 
Handel's "Concerto Grosso op. 6 
No , 11 " and Mozart ' s 
"Divertimento III. K269" under 
the direction of Thomas Nee. 

On Saturday evening. the 
James Emery/ Robert Dick Duo 
will perform a special evening of 
creative mu ic at the Cent r for 
Music Experiment at UCSD. The 
duo perform original 
compo itions and improvisa-
tions for a wide array of guitars, 
flutes and electronics. 

James Emery and Robert Dick 
combine acoustic instrumental 
virtuosity with original use of 
amplification and electronic 
transformation of sound. 
Drawing on diversified 
backgrounds and musical 
traditions. they have reached a 

[TH"E AOVENTURES OF ( 
fT'S #It .A.... IT', /Ill 'O,T 1,,"' $ 

-University Bookstore 

lewl of artistic development 
that is a coherent. original 
whole - not the sum of 
innurnces. 

They have played together 
since 1979. and have toured in 
France. Belgium and Holland. as 
well as in the US. Both Emery 
and Dick hve received critical 
acclaim as unique, innovative 
performer. 

Emery has performed with 
Leroy Jenkins. Anthony Braxton. 
Muhal Richard Abrams. and 
Richard Teitelbaum. He is a 
founding member of the String 
Trio of New York and has 

recorded for Black Saint. JCO.\ 
and Otil Records. Emery aho 
leads his own ensemble and 
Quartet as well as presenting 
solo concert . 

Dick has performed with 
Steve 14cy. Richard Teitelbaum. 
Bobby Naughton and many 
others. and hCl toured in Europ 
and Scandanavia playing solo 
concerts. 

This concert is the last of the 
Duo's California tour. which 
included performances at the 
San francisco Conservatory. the 
Arnold Schoenberg Institute at 
USc. and at UCLA.

AMI j Voit Ultimate 
Disc Classic 

It was bi lled as the 1 st Annual 
AMF /VOlT Ultimate Disc Classic and it 
really wasn't what you'd expect of a 
1st annual. Ho-hum, you think? Wrong! 
This first annual was exciting stuff. 

Eight "totally into it" ultimate disc 
teams battled It out last Sunday on the 
Pryatel fields for the right to hold up 
their Index fingers for the next year. 
The Intramural Coed Ultimate 
championships were the occasion, 
but the real showcase was the sport 
of Ultimate Disc, itself 

ThiS game is definitely a sport and It 
definitely takes talent and ability. And 
naturally, the UCSD 1M Program Will 
take the brunt of It As soon as 
everyOf1e discovers the exhilaration of 
the game, UCSD 1M'S Will be out of 
control again Another 1000 teams 
Will be shOWing up, and the 1M Czars 
Will once again rent out all of the 
plaYing fields In Arizona Just to keep 
things gOing. 

The AMF /VOlT people Jumped Into 
the act thiS year to help promote their 
new 'Vector" Ultimate diSC. They 
definitely did their homework. The 
top players on campus had nothing 
but good things to say about the new 
heaVier ridged disc. And of course, 
the free championship T-Shirts that 
they gave out didn't hurt a bit either. 

ThiS quarter's proud wearers were 
not the bashful sort. Indiscretion (7-0) 
waltzed through the Coed AA 
Championship with a hard-earned 7-5 
semi-final win over Fudge, and a solid 
11-4 thumping of ChriS Knigge's Big 
DISks In the championship game, 
Indiscretion was led by the "1M TWinS" 
Karen lamp and Lynn Rudman who 
had 5 and 3 scores respectively on the 
afternoon 

It was another feather In the skull 
cap for Lamp, Rudman and the rest of 
their med school cronies, who are 
having a bdnner year In IMs so far 
They've already won Ultimate, 
Waterpolo, and Team Te'1nlS and are 
looking tor more next quarter 

OK, girls, we know you can win at 
athletics.. but the Budman really 
wdnts to know If you can take out hiS 
appendiX when he needs It 

The Coed A Ultimate champions 
proved to be another band of 1M 
groupies. Jay Richards, Ken Nordling, 
Peter Kim and the clan squeezed 
plenty of ultimate diSC and football 
Into their weekend. 

Their "Untouchables' Ultimate team 
scrambled to the title With an 8-6 
semifinal win over the George 
Fishbeck Fan Club and an 11 6 
thumping of the Ultl-mates In the title 
garre But, unfortunately, their 
championship party was short·lived. 
After two sWigs of hiS long· neck Bud, 
Capt J R Superstar anXiously 
announced to hiS exhausted 
teammates, '('mon, gang, drink 
up,we've got another football game 
over at MUir " 

The timing of hiS announcement 
wasn't real good The last we saw of 
him, good 01' JR. was trucking through 
the woods near Central library. HIS 
"former" teammates were hotly In 
pursuit

In.-rtube Waterpolo 
Championships 

The annual 1M Waterpolo 
Championships at UCSD have 
traditionally been boisterous affairs. 
And last Monday night's party at the 
pool was no different. 

For some mysterious reason, UCSD 
students splashing around at midnight 
In rubber doughnuts has always 
attracted a crowd, As In SRO 
crazy .... but then, that's UCSD, folks 

ThiS year's championship crowd 
was as noisy and demonstrative as 
ever. One team even brought 
cheerleaders With stunt cards. All 
were there to discover the Inevitable. 
Who was gOing to win the AAA, AA 
and A championships for 1982. 

They needn't have bothered to 
show up. All the results could have 
been mailed In 

Although the games were 
competetlve, the outcomes were 
never In doubt. Pump and Shoot (7-2) 
led by John Brody and Sue Wilson 
cruised to an 8-5 win over the Water 
Babies to annex the 'A " title It was 
their 4th straight playoff win of the 
week. 

The pace became a bit more funous 
dUring the "AA" title match, but the 
result was just as predictable. The MD 
Tubees, a bu nch of ringer med school 
school students recruited by Karin 
Feldman, kept the previously 
unbeated Aqua Cows at bay for 30 
minutes running, The final score of 12-
8 was not indicative of its closeness. 
Former Stanford Ali-American Alan 
Mouchawar flipped In 5 goals at Will 
and could have had two dozen more. 

In the big one ... "AAA ..... the finalists 
were pretty much regulars One of 
them, SKUF, had been there plenty of 
times before at least a dozen And as 
usual they finished second best 

ThiS time around they tried an 
alternating goalie strategy. And as 
usual It backfired. Led by Gill Bolt, 
Bonnie Bp.tz, and Bnan Lanvlere, the 
Gear Heads (5· 1) made SWISS cheese 
out of SKUF's goaltenders and swam 
away With an 11·4 VictOry

per week.

and a BA in Managemen t degrees for relevant 
life learning experiences. 

¥ An accredi ted university known for 75 years 
excellence. Bachelor's applicants should have 
approximately two years of acceptable transfer 
credit. The MA in Management is open to 
qualified persons holding a Bachelor's degree.

~Where.ll Your Son or Daughter Going to Live Next Year?-
It's no secret that on-campus housing is getting 
more and more difficult to find, and the cost of 
dormitory living is skyrocketing. 

Are you looking for an alternative to expensive, 

campus controlled housing for the students in 
your family? Could a 2 bedroom, 1 Y2 bath 
townhouse within walking distance of the 
UCSD campus be the alternative you're looking 
for? -

If you answered yes to these questions, let me tell you more about just such a condo. 
It's located at 3193-A Evening Way in La Jolla (just off Gilman Drive). The complex is 
beautifi,JIIy kept and has two pools and jacuzzis. The condo itself has a patio and a 
balconY; a 2 car garage, laundry hook-ups, and all kitchen appliances, including a 

microwave.

FlNANCING: ___ 1ocx, down, 30 year tenn and 10% for the first three years and 15% for 

the remaining 17 years,

Also, should you rent a room to some other student, substantial benefits may be 
derived from this as an income property.

Thinking of a 
Communication Major? 

Better Think Fast!! 
Starting on January 14, the communicatIon major will bt 

open only to those students who have completed a 
uPre .. Communication major" 

with a grade of "C" or better. This will consist of the present 
lower divi ion pre~requisites and Comm/Gen 20. 

Students may declare a Communication major before the 
January deadline by filling out a blue change of major card 
available at the Communication office. For your 
convenience, the Department will ubmit the e cards to the 
Registrar. 

PRESENT MAJORS!! 
We urge present Communication major to check theIr 10 
card or the Spring '82 grades to verify that they are declared 
a a major. If in doubt, check at the Communication Office. 
InformatIon about the c.urrent prt:~requisite and about the 
rrt ~commUnI arton major I aVaIlable in the bin outside the 
CommunIcation Office.
